  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2df91e6c-24a9-4967-bb74-9c5ddd54a8ac'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer9745885229880762726">In the early days of the Civil War, rumors of gold in the frozen Klondike brought hordes of newcomers to the Pacific Northwest.   <span id="freeText9745885229880762726" style="display:none">In the early days of the Civil War, rumors of gold in the frozen Klondike brought hordes of newcomers to the Pacific Northwest. Anxious to compete, Russian prospectors commissioned inventor Leviticus Blue to create a great machine that could mine through Alaska’s ice. Thus was Dr. Blue’s Incredible Bone-Shaking Drill Engine born.<br /><br />But on its first test run the Boneshaker went terribly awry, destroying several blocks of downtown Seattle and unearthing a subterranean vein of blight gas that turned anyone who breathed it into the living dead.<br /><br />Now it is sixteen years later, and a wall has been built to enclose the devastated and toxic city. Just beyond it lives Blue’s widow, Briar Wilkes. Life is hard with a ruined reputation and a teenaged boy to support, but she and Ezekiel are managing. Until Ezekiel undertakes a secret crusade to rewrite history.<br /><br />His quest will take him under the wall and into a city teeming with ravenous undead, air pirates, criminal overlords, and heavily armed refugees. And only Briar can bring him out alive.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Great representation of Steampunk - sense of place and feel of the era, story line is consistent with the era, and the language is carefully crafted t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Great representation of Steampunk - sense of place and feel of the era, story line is consistent with the era, and the language is carefully crafted to fit the era. Other books: The Parasol Protectorate series by Gail Carriger, Leviathan series by Scott Westerfield, Infernal Devises series by Cassandra Claire, Ministry of Peculiar Occurances by Pip Ballentine, Magnificent Devises by Shelley Adina.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_91338657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91338657" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036930-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583425448p2/1036930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91338657?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1036930-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=fiction-that-speculates">fiction-that-speculates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=most-popular-reviews">most-popular-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91338657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14174414670476809768">``Miss Eliza Bennet, let me persuade you to follow my example, and take a turn about the room. -- I assure you the anti-gravity hoverchannel is very refreshing after sitting so long in one attitude.''<br/> <br/>Eliza was surprised, but agreed to it immediately. She unstrapt herself from her leather seat restraints and stood, careful to maintain her balance as the airship encountered turbulence. When she entered the hoverchannel, she activated the polarity redistribution magnets within her combat suit and </span>
  <span id="freeText14174414670476809768" style="display:none">``Miss Eliza Bennet, let me persuade you to follow my example, and take a turn about the room. -- I assure you the anti-gravity hoverchannel is very refreshing after sitting so long in one attitude.''<br /> <br />Eliza was surprised, but agreed to it immediately. She unstrapt herself from her leather seat restraints and stood, careful to maintain her balance as the airship encountered turbulence. When she entered the hoverchannel, she activated the polarity redistribution magnets within her combat suit and began floating comfortably around the perimeter of the foyer.<br /> <br />Miss Bingley's attention was quite engaged in watching Mr. Darcy's progress through his book, so much so that at one point she nearly navigated the ship into the side of Pemberley; and she was perpetually making some inquiry.<br /> <br />At length, finally exhausted by her tenacious attempts to force a conversation regarding his book, Darcy relented. "It's entitled Boneshaker. An American novel."<br /> <br />"What do you think of it?" Eliza said as she drifted by. <br /> <br />"A bit nonsensical, really. Steampunk claptrap about the Civil War going on much longer than it actually did, which caused technological advances that didn't really happen until much later. And a zombie-infested city called Seattle. It has been blocked off from the rest of the country, and our heroine must go in to rescue her foolish son." <br /> <br />Mr. Bingley crossed the room, his steam-powered mechanical legs stomping their way across the carpet to the cabinet where he refilled his glass. "Zombies in America? That does sound quite silly. Everyone knows that zombies are native to Britain. That's how I lost my legs."<br /> <br />"Please, Bingley, don't tell us that old story again," Mr. Hurst said, adjusting himself on the sofa before falling back asleep.<br /> <br />Darcy said, "The plot moves along at a good pace, but the characters are a bit uninspired. A teenage boy constantly doing something inadvisable; the protective mother, blasting zombies and trying to save him."<br /> <br />Eliza smiled. "Darcy, certainly you aren't saying literature is full of strong female characters who run around rescuing male characters."<br /> <br />"Nor should it be," Mr. Hurst said, drifting slowly in and out of consciousness.<br /> <br />Ignoring Mr. Hurst's interjection, Darcy said, "I suppose the fairer sex aren't shown in powerful roles that often, even in these books written in the far future about the distant past . . . er, or perhaps about the same time as now . . . When were we written?"<br /> <br />Miss Bingley inquired, "Are you sure the dinner agreed with you?"<br /> <br />"I feel fine, thank you," Darcy said. <br /> <br />"Admit it," Sherlock Holmes said, standing in the doorway, Watson at his side. "You enjoy all the fashionable gimmicks flying left and right, and the pace keeps you entertained. Yet you wonder why nothing surprising was done with any of these elements."<br /> <br />Darcy moved over as Holmes sat on the sofa beside him, lighting a pipe. "You're right, Holmes. The whole reinvention of the Civil War is fascinating in theory. Then the author does nothing with it. The book has nothing to say. No reflections on the civil war, racism, or politics. Nor does it say anything about the true nature of zombies. In fact, it says little about love, which is the very heart of the story."<br /> <br />J. K. Rowling, refilling her glass of zinfandel, said, "And it's practically a young adult novel, isn't it? Other than one or two mildly violent zombie moments and one four letter 'S' word, this could be the next film from Pixar. There's not even a gay sorcerer to throw off the prudes." <br /> <br />Darcy met Eliza's eyes as she orbited the room. "Have you read it as well, Miss Bennett?"<br /> <br />"Braaaains," Mr. Hurst moaned softly.<br /><br />"I found it diverting," Eliza said. "I always read the books nominated for the Nebula awards. But, like you, I found the novel didn't meet my expectations. When you look beyond the stylish trappings, you have a run-of-the-mill adventure story written in a workmanlike fashion. I imagine the query letter was spectacular, though."<br /> <br />Darcy was on the verge of speaking when Mr. Hurst lunged up from the sofa, saliva splattering from his vicious maw, his eyes sunken in and rolled back into his head. He lurched across the room toward Bingley, whose back was facing him.<br /> <br />Eliza kicked off of the wall and rolled over to Darcy, pulling his pistol from his belt, and fired several rounds through Mr. Hurst's head. A splatter of blood, brain and skull chips showered down on Harold Bloom.<br /> <br />"Well," Mr. Harold Bloom said, wiping blood from his face and wiping it on the sofa, "that was entirely unnecessary, but what HASN'T been? The whole book review is sound and fury, signifying nothing. And how many times is this hack going to parody <u>Pride and Prejudice</u>? He seems to think it's much more funny than it is, just as Oscar Wilde thought himself hilarious, when he is in fact highly over-esteemed."<br /> <br />Holmes puffed his pipe, a gray cloud of smoke rising above him. "I can't believe I didn't notice Mr. Hurst was turning. Usually I'm so attentive to details."<br /> <br />"Nobody's perfect," Darcy said. "Would you mind putting that pipe out? We are in a zeppelin, you know."<br /> <br />Holmes sighed and stood up, pulling on his overcoat. "I'm going next door to the Kurt Vonnegut review. Pipe smoking is encouraged over there." <br /> <br />And as Holmes left the room, suddenly the review stopped.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14174414670476809768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_94097600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94097600" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94097600?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94097600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3998818391633882363">(1.5)<br/><br/>Steampunk and zombies and mini-apocalypse, oh my. How could you go wrong?<br/><br/>For starters, you could have lead characters that I never really connected with or cared that much about. Protagonists whose most active role was to get themselves into the city, and then who became fortunes of fate, as things happened to them. <br/><br/>I did like some of the secondary characters better, especially Swakhammer. (Though it seemed weird to me that Briar called calling him Mr. Swakhammer. It was probably meant to b</span>
  <span id="freeText3998818391633882363" style="display:none">(1.5)<br /><br />Steampunk and zombies and mini-apocalypse, oh my. How could you go wrong?<br /><br />For starters, you could have lead characters that I never really connected with or cared that much about. Protagonists whose most active role was to get themselves into the city, and then who became fortunes of fate, as things happened to them. <br /><br />I did like some of the secondary characters better, especially Swakhammer. (Though it seemed weird to me that Briar called calling him Mr. Swakhammer. It was probably meant to be an affectation to remind us of the time period, when men and women were more formal, but since these characters are so informal, it was just kind of weird. Just another layer of distance in a book which keeps you at yours...<br /><br />I think, really, that's what it is. The characters are never really developed - it's more an actiony-adventure type story, which could be fine, except it seemed like it almost wanted to be a deeper, more thoughtful story at times, it just never quite managed to be so.<br /><br />Oh, and the brown font on the off-white paper killed me at first, but I did mostly get used to it.<br /><br />Anyway, I never felt truly frightened or saddened for these characters and their exploits, though I did sometimes feel annoyed that they seemed so ingrateful for the help people were giving them (Briar), and that they kept running off and getting themselves in trouble without finding out what was going on first (Zeke). And I never really connected with them, so didn't much care.<br /><br />And the whole thing with the big bad was meh. And I don't just mean the anti-climactic end, I mean everything about it. The build-up, the reveal, everything. There's something which happens at the end which Briar is said not to care about because her focus is on something else. Well, I didn't care, either. <br /><br />Wow - do you think I could say "I didn't care" any more? <br /><br />The only thing I did sort of care about is the fate of Swahkhammer, which we're left not knowing. I read somewhere that this is the first of a planned trilogy, but I doubt I'll continue unless I hear really good things about the follow-up. <br /><br />All that said, I do agree with one reviewer who said that this story could make a good movie, though. Visually it would be pretty awesome, and you can get away with less develoepd characters and more haphazard happenings in movies.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3998818391633882363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82748775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82748775" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82748775?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=christmas-gift">christmas-gift</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82748775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4659834452561569824">Sixteen years after Leviticus Blue reputedly robbed a string of banks and released the Blight using his drilling machine, the Boneshaker, his son Ezekiel goes back into the walled remains of Seattle, braving rotters and Doornails, to clear his name. His mother, Briar Wilkes, goes into the walled wasteland to bring him out. Can she find Zeke before Dr. Minnericht finds him?<br/><br/>I've got mixed feelings about this one. For one thing, the writing doesn't tickle my innards and the characters are all prett</span>
  <span id="freeText4659834452561569824" style="display:none">Sixteen years after Leviticus Blue reputedly robbed a string of banks and released the Blight using his drilling machine, the Boneshaker, his son Ezekiel goes back into the walled remains of Seattle, braving rotters and Doornails, to clear his name. His mother, Briar Wilkes, goes into the walled wasteland to bring him out. Can she find Zeke before Dr. Minnericht finds him?<br /><br />I've got mixed feelings about this one. For one thing, the writing doesn't tickle my innards and the characters are all pretty weak. It also feels like it could have been 70 or 80 pages shorter. A steampunk book with zombies and airships shouldn't have so many dull spots. Also, there was a 35 page block missing from my copy but I don't think I missed a whole lot due to the aforementioned pacing issues. Furthermore, Boneshaker is a misleading title since the Boneshaker doesn't make an appearance until the very end.<br /><br />However, I did manage to enjoy myself while reading it. I love the idea of a walled up city infested by zombies as well as the culture of those that stayed behind to live off of what was left, the Doornails. The concept of zombies being created by subterranean pockets of gas was interesting, as was lemon sap, the drug made from said gas. The steampunk tech was nicely done, complete with artificial limbs and a sound cannon. The airships were also good, even if under-utilized. Zeke and Briar's struggle to find one another was well done, even if it dragged for my tastes. Dr. Minnericht was a Darth Vader-ish enemy but the reveal of his identity was pretty good, as was his death.<br /><br />I wouldn't exactly say I'd recommend buying this but if you could find someone to lend it to you, I don't think you'll be very disappointed.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4659834452561569824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77991902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11599769239668429151"><b>Posted at <a href='http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2016/03/boneshaker.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelf Inflicted</a></b> <br/><br/>Dazzling inventions, air pirates, evil bad guys, underground vaults, goggles, daring rescues, gold, Blight gas, a one-armed bartender, a princess, zombies. Oh, what fun! <br/><br/>The setting was vividly described and rich in details. The main characters were well developed and fascinating. Briar Wilkes, widow of Leviticus Blue, eccentric inventor, searches for her teenage son, Zeke, in a walled-off section of Seattle, where a dangerous yellow gas shrouds the city, forcing the re</span>
  <span id="freeText11599769239668429151" style="display:none"><b>Posted at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2016/03/boneshaker.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a></b> <br /><br />Dazzling inventions, air pirates, evil bad guys, underground vaults, goggles, daring rescues, gold, Blight gas, a one-armed bartender, a princess, zombies. Oh, what fun! <br /><br />The setting was vividly described and rich in details. The main characters were well developed and fascinating. Briar Wilkes, widow of Leviticus Blue, eccentric inventor, searches for her teenage son, Zeke, in a walled-off section of Seattle, where a dangerous yellow gas shrouds the city, forcing the remaining inhabitants to live underground. Lots of action, suspense, and vibrant, quirky characters helped move the story along at a brisk pace. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed the twists, surprises, and very satisfying ending of this riveting adventure story. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2479353632742162196">1) Best cover art I've seen in a LONG TIME!<br/><br/>2) Very specific style of writing that too a while to hook me.   <span id="freeText2479353632742162196" style="display:none">1) Best cover art I've seen in a LONG TIME!<br /><br />2) Very specific style of writing that too a while to hook me. It reminded me of Red Dead Redemption in book form with Steampunk. I definitely got into it when all the zombie stuff took off, cool details there.<br />3) All the Steampunk stuff was awesome, and well detailed and realized. The world definitely grew on me a lot.<br />4) Main problem was that the characters didn't hook me until WAAAY into the book. I really feel like the main character could have been fleshed out more, maybe it was the spare prose style that kept me a bit distanced from caring enough? I dunno. I never really felt like her backstory with her dad and husband was filled to my satisfaction, it almost felt coincidental that she was tied to two such famous people in this world, maybe it's my fault and I skimmed too much though. I did love the fact that she wasn't a cliched "peppy go-getter lady lead who meets a dreamy airship captain". So kudos for a different woman lead there. <br /><br />Definitely recommended for an interesting, Western-style Steampunk extravaganza.</span>

<div id="review_99890392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99890392" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=doing-the-dishes">doing-the-dishes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99890392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16082449820256353455">I dug <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/221253.Cherie_Priest' title='Cherie Priest' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cherie Priest</a>’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Boneshaker' title='Boneshaker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Boneshaker</a>, but I wanted so much more. <br/><br/>I dug Blighted Seattle and the Outskirts, but I wanted more detail in the former and more time in the latter.<br/><br/>I dug the Rotters, but I wanted more rot, more zombie madness, and more exploration of their potential ability to communicate and problem solve.<br/><br/>I dug the pseudo-history and Hale Quarter, the fictional biographer, but I wanted more installments of his history.<br/><br/>I dug the back story of Leviticus Blue, but I wanted to be convinced th</span>
  <span id="freeText16082449820256353455" style="display:none">I dug <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/221253.Cherie_Priest" title="Cherie Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherie Priest</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Boneshaker" title="Boneshaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Boneshaker</a>, but I wanted so much more. <br /><br />I dug Blighted Seattle and the Outskirts, but I wanted more detail in the former and more time in the latter.<br /><br />I dug the Rotters, but I wanted more rot, more zombie madness, and more exploration of their potential ability to communicate and problem solve.<br /><br />I dug the pseudo-history and Hale Quarter, the fictional biographer, but I wanted more installments of his history.<br /><br />I dug the back story of Leviticus Blue, but I wanted to be convinced that he was evil rather than merely devastatingly irresponsible because while I can see devastatingly irresponsible as being negative for all, I don’t think it can really be called evil.<br /><br />I dug Dr. Minnerecht, but I wanted more time in his lair, more time with his nasty deeds, and way less of his silly petulance.<br /><br />I dug Zeke, but I wanted him to do more, to be more active.<br /><br />I dug how Briar took responsibility for the killing of Levi Blue, but I didn’t like that she did it nor the way that she did it, and I find the general cheering on of her actions a bit disconcerting.<br /><br />I liked the supporting cast, but I wanted more of what brought them to where they were, what motivated them, what they cared about, who they were pre- &amp; post-Blight.<br /><br />I dug the technological steampunk elements, and was more than willing to suspend my disbelief, but I wanted more of the steampunk social criticism to go along with the toys.<br /><br />I dug the hints of a larger world beyond Seattle, but I wish there’d been more of it here so I wouldn’t have to wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670800.Clementine__The_Clockwork_Century___2_" title="Clementine (The Clockwork Century, #2) by Cherie Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">Clementine</a>.<br /><br />I dug that there were three interesting women, but I didn’t like their disdain for men nor that they felt like three versions of the same woman. <br /><br />I dug the dirigibles, and for once there was enough time with the Skypirates to fulfill my desire.<br /><br />So to recap: I dug it, but...<br /></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_175603391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175603391" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175603391?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=nebula">nebula</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175603391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13363386129118704820"><br/><br/>Started off slow, but I fully realize that was a miscalibration with the story compatibility recognizer. I don't really do the mother-hen story line, and I often get the urge to slap headstrong teenage boys. I started this on vacation in NYC, and we just weren't getting along. Plus, NYC is all busy and distracting and such. Once home, I picked it back up and had a little better luck, but soon got distracted with <s>shinier books</s> life. Finally opened it again today and finished the last 250 or so pa</span>
  <span id="freeText13363386129118704820" style="display:none"><br /><br />Started off slow, but I fully realize that was a miscalibration with the story compatibility recognizer. I don't really do the mother-hen story line, and I often get the urge to slap headstrong teenage boys. I started this on vacation in NYC, and we just weren't getting along. Plus, NYC is all busy and distracting and such. Once home, I picked it back up and had a little better luck, but soon got distracted with <s>shinier books</s> life. Finally opened it again today and finished the last 250 or so pages, proving at least one of two things: 1) that I am a ridiculous procrastinator that would do anything other than class homework, and 2) Priest can pull it together; it just takes awhile. <br /><br />Story alternates between the viewpoint of Ezekiel, a young teen, and that of his mother, Briar Wilkes, a hard-working widow. She was married to an inventor, Leviticus Blue, who built a machine that was supposed to impress the Russians with it's gold-mining skill. Except before the debut, things go a little haywire and a bank or two is robbed instead, and a mysterious low-lying gas released into the local atmosphere. Perhaps it was connected to the machine, perhaps it wasn't. Blue disappeared, and the gas turned everyone it touched into "rotters," otherwise known as <s>coffee-deprived Seattleans</s> zombies. The rest of the world walled Seattle off and did their best to forget about it, except for two things: they still hate Briar, as a stand-in for Blue; and the yellow gas can be distilled into a drug (<i>of course</i> the new drug comes through Seattle. Don't they always? ). Zeke decides to find out the truth. Mama hen chases him down with the intention of making him safe, and perhaps, telling him the truth.<br /><br />Positives: characterization that is fairly multi-culti without making it an <i>issue</i> and doesn't treat females like a bunch of sex objects (<i>cough, cough, Brent Weeks</i>), but instead like <i>people</i> trying to live how they know, and be as tough as they need to to survive. Side characters were particularly interesting and unique, and I rather liked they they didn't always 'group up' and stay together for the rest of the <s>quest</s> search. I'm particularly fond of the Indian Princess who was oracle-like in her advice, and mysterious enough that Zeke wasn't sure if she was going to knife him or save him.<br /><br />Criticisms: Blah, airships. I suppose they are useful for getting characters in and out of walled cities. Personally, I find them to be the steampunk equivalent of the modern car chase, and usually use the time to go <s>fix</s> get a drink. Blah fifteen year old boys, who are at once brave, naive, selfish, defiant, clever and obtuse.<br /><br />Of all the characters, the villain was a bit of a trope. Build-up was scary; actuality was a bit like Paul Reubens in the original <i>Buffy</i>. I also could have passed on the conceit of the weird dude in the beginning approaching Briar about writing a biography. Not sure where it got the story, except some navel-gazingness. Might have incited the kid to leave, but then again, it might not have. Oh wait, I get it. It was a way to introduce backstory. Ok, I'll scratch that as a complaint. Annoyed me at the end, however. <br /><br />Speaking of the end, it was a strange mix-up of unfinished and happily ever after (oh stop, that didn't give anything away). Quite a few unanswered questions. While part of me likes to have everything explained, it just isn't possible in a book of this length; I was left with intriguing questions about the Blight, about the Civil War, and about the people in Seattle.<br /><br />Overall, a middling book that I'm glad I read. Judging by the way reviews run the star gamut, it might be worth checking out for yourself. And I still can't decide if Priest pulled it together or I'm a <s>successful</s> horrible procrastinator. <br /><br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/07/13/boneshaker-by-cherie-priest-maybe-tingled/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13363386129118704820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1223367532028611414" style="display:none">2.5 stars. I liked the set up of this steampunk story and I thought the characters were well developed (especially Briar who I thought was great). That said, for some reason I did not get "hooked" on the story and found myself just getting through the book. For me, I would have liked to have learned more about the "alternate" world in which the book is set in and have the story tie into (or at least hint at) bigger issues to come. There were some nice tidbits about the larger world but I would have liked to have seen more. All and all, it was a decent read and I will read the next book in the series when it comes out where the story will hopefully expand.<br /><br />Nominee: Hugo Award for Best Novel <br />Nominee: Nebula Award for Best Novel </span>

<div id="review_326273584" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326273584" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326273584?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction-stand-alone">science-fiction-stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=locus-sci-fi">locus-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-2000s">pub-2000s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326273584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12585390647584746503"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Christmas 2010: I realised that I had got stuck in a rut. I was re-reading old favourites again and again, waiting for a few trusted authors to release new works. Something had to be done.<br/><br/>On the spur of the moment I set myself a challenge, to read every book to have won the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Sci-Fi</a> award. That’s 35 books, 6 of which I’d previously read, leaving 29 titles by 14 authors who were new to me.<br/><br/>While working through this reading list I got married, went on my honeymoon, switched career and beca</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12585390647584746503" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Christmas 2010: I realised that I had got stuck in a rut. I was re-reading old favourites again and again, waiting for a few trusted authors to release new works. Something had to be done.<br><br>On the spur of the moment I set myself a challenge, to read every book to have won the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Sci-Fi</a> award. That’s 35 books, 6 of which I’d previously read, leaving 29 titles by 14 authors who were new to me.<br><br>While working through this reading list I got married, went on my honeymoon, switched career and became a father. As such these stories became imprinted on my memory as the soundtrack to the happiest period in my life (so far).</b><br><br>I don’t know about you, but sometimes I save the best part of my dinner until last – savouring the anticipation as much as the taste. <b>
  <i>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1137215.Boneshaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Boneshaker</a>
  </i>
</b> (the 2010 winner of the Locus Sci-Fi Award) had the look, to me, of a tasty little treat, so I kept putting it off for as long as I could resist.<br><br>Steampunk, zombies and air-pirates. Sounds perfect, doesn’t it?<br>When I saw that the text inside is printed in sepia-brown, I thought it was a delightful touch of icing on the cake!<br><br>Gushing reviews like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72293575" rel="nofollow noopener">this one</a>, from the usually more reserved Jason, didn’t dampen my growing expectations.<br><br>We all read a lot of books, hoping to find 'A BOOK'. <br>Sadly, for me, <b>
  <i>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1137215.Boneshaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Boneshaker</a>
  </i>
</b> is just ‘a book’.<br><br>Before I start my grumbling, I’d like to acknowledge the many things that Priest does well here:<br>-	The original concept is brilliant<br>-	The book tumbles along at a good pace<br>-	Much of the imagery is strong and memorable<br>-	Several of the supporting characters stand out brightly<br> 	(I'm thinking of Swakhammer, Lucy O'Gunning and Fang)<br><br>So far, so good?<br><br>My first big issue comes with the Mother/Son protagonists (Briar &amp; Zeke). I can’t think of many <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(any?) YA protagonists blander than Zeke. His original decision to go into the city seems poorly motivated and once he gets there the only memorable character trait he demonstrates is his resilient politeness (and lack of initiative) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. As for Briar, she’s got a touch more <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[depth (stubborn, reticent, can shoot well, etc) but is still a long way from sparkling characterisation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>My second issue is the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[lack of control either of them have over their grand adventure. From the moment they get inside Zombieburg they’re either kidnapped or rescued – led from pillar to post, following behind like meek little lambkins. The most difficult choices they make are ( if / when / in which direction / how fast ) to run away <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!<br><br>My final gripe made me so mad that when I saw my cats had knocked the book into a bathtub full of water shortly after I’d finished it, I didn’t think “Oh no, my treasured novel has been soaked!” – I thought “Hah! You deserved that!”<br><br>There are two major hooks and two minor hooks to pull us towards the climax.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>1)	MAJOR: Will Briar find and rescue her son?<br>2)	MAJOR: Is evil Dr Minnerich really Briar’s long-lost hubby, Levi Blue?<br>3)	MINOR: Did Blue go on the rampage which released the blight deliberately?<br>4)	MINOR: Why has Briar stuck around Zombieburg outskirts ever since?<br><br>Number 1) is never really in doubt. The books not got enough edge to risk killing either of the protags.<br><br>2, 3 &amp; 4 all implode like a slug in a pressure chamber. <br><br>YES – Blue went on the rampage that released the blight!<br>NO – Minnericht is not Blue, Briar shot Blue years ago!<br>Briar has in fact known this all along and could have cleared up the mystery by simply telling… anyone at any point…<br>But she didn’t tell because… I’m not sure?<br><br>We’re bludgeoned with the fact that she’s despised in the Outskirts because she was married to Blue who was thought to have released the blight. Surely confirming this, and that she killed him for it, would have gone a long way to restoring her reputation?<br><br>Maybe she was keeping schtum because of the stolen money she squirreled away?<br>Oh no, wait – she seems to have forgotten all about that until right at the end. <br><br>We never get a decent reason for why she never left the outskirts. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Frankly, by the end I didn’t care.<br><br>I enjoyed the ride – it was a kind of 2.5 for me, and I’m a generous soul so I rounded it up to a 3 – but as I was hoping for a 4, I left <b>
  <i>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1137215.Boneshaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Boneshaker</a>
  </i>
</b> sorely disappointed.<br><br>ps - I just remembered that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Princess knew all along who evil Dr M really was, and just didn't fancy telling anyone <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and also that we never get a good (any?) explanation for why <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Chinamen stay to run the bellows <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - <b>gah!</b><br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329913150" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12585390647584746503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5759012775303932592"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448413487i/17136214._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='241' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I rarely (because I'm cheap and OCD) abandon a book. It may take me awhile, but eventually the constant chirp in the back of my brain makes me run and pick the damn thing up and just finish it. However, there are few RARE exceptions to this rule. <br/><br/>When a book is SO poorly written, so filled with cliches, bad adjectives, and weak verbs; when the dialogue is so awkward and stilted that it is a painful experience to read; when the book produces no virtuous feelings in me; when there is NO forward mo</span>
  <span id="freeText5759012775303932592" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448413487i/17136214._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="241" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I rarely (because I'm cheap and OCD) abandon a book. It may take me awhile, but eventually the constant chirp in the back of my brain makes me run and pick the damn thing up and just finish it. However, there are few RARE exceptions to this rule. <br><br>When a book is SO poorly written, so filled with cliches, bad adjectives, and weak verbs; when the dialogue is so awkward and stilted that it is a painful experience to read; when the book produces no virtuous feelings in me; when there is NO forward momentum (except for the earthy desire to finish and be done with it) -- it begins to dawn on me (pg 194) that I should just abandon the book. <br><br>Thus I excommunicate it: close the book, blow out the candle, and ring the damn bell. May god have mercy on Cherie Priest's soul.</span>

<div id="review_1065660336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1065660336" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065660336?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781429942492" href="/book/show/7294675-boneshaker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=setting-1800s">setting-1800s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=award-winner">award-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-i-dropped">series-i-dropped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=setting-america">setting-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=bleak-or-melancholy">bleak-or-melancholy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=published-2000s">published-2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=grim-gritty">grim-gritty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065660336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6325268378074129224"><i>Boneshaker</i> is very different from other Steampunk books that I've read (and enjoyed). I think it's considered Steampunk because there are airships (not enough, though!) and a few machines that could be considered in the historical Sci Fi realm. Other than that, it does not have any of the characteristics that I look forward to in Steampunk. No adventure. No cool gadgets or scientific experiments (the breathing masks just don't count). <br/><br/>And there's far too much grit and gore. I've never really bee</span>
  <span id="freeText6325268378074129224" style="display:none"><i>Boneshaker</i> is very different from other Steampunk books that I've read (and enjoyed). I think it's considered Steampunk because there are airships (not enough, though!) and a few machines that could be considered in the historical Sci Fi realm. Other than that, it does not have any of the characteristics that I look forward to in Steampunk. No adventure. No cool gadgets or scientific experiments (the breathing masks just don't count). <br /><br />And there's far too much grit and gore. I've never really been interested in zombies. They make a boring enemy, in my mind. This book only confirmed that. Far too much of it is spent running from 'rotters' or shooting them. When I realized it was a zombie book, I knew I was in for a challenge. <br /><br />This is an apocalyptic dystopia set in the past with some barely recognizable Steampunk elements. It's the bleakest dystopia I've read so far, one where people can't even breathe the air. Most of the time not spent running from rotters is spent trying to breathe through masks that filter out the yellow sludge that turns people into rotters. Let's just say this is not a pleasant place to be. And let's say that unpleasant things happen when people are unable to take their masks off for any reason. Too much time is spent on every little detail of how hard it is to get by there, on details I'd really like to get out of my head somehow.<br /><br />I could have used more focus on the people and their interactions, because that's when it started to get more interesting (in the last quarter of the book). <br /><br />I'm actually not sure why I'm giving this a second star. Maybe because I managed to finish it and was actually ok with the ending? Or maybe I liked a couple of the characters (not the main ones), even though I didn't get enough of them. But I really didn't enjoy the experience of reading it much at all and I'm glad it's over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6325268378074129224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77556096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77556096" />
    <a title="Cassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2282938-cassy"><img alt="Cassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565892954p2/2282938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77556096?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassy" href="/user/show/2282938-cassy">Cassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=physical-own">physical-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=fiction-scifi-fantasy-paranormal">fiction-scifi-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=event-met-author">event-met-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=region-america-canada">region-america-canada</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77556096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6843132328336388043">This was my first foray into steampunk – unless <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119322.The_Golden_Compass__His_Dark_Materials___1_' title='The Golden Compass (His Dark Materials, #1) by Philip Pullman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Golden Compass</a> counts. This may not be my genre. I am willing to keep going for a book or two, but the prospects are poor. And according to the clerk at the bookstore, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6381205.Soulless__The_Parasol_Protectorate___1_' title='Soulless (The Parasol Protectorate, #1) by Gail Carriger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Soulless</a> <i>must</i> be my next read.<br/><br/>I was on the fence about reading this one. It was officially on my to-read list, but the ho-hum reviews were making me doubt the placement. Then I heard Cherie Priest was coming to a local bookstore, Murder by the Book (great name, right?) in a week. I t</span>
  <span id="freeText6843132328336388043" style="display:none">This was my first foray into steampunk – unless <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119322.The_Golden_Compass__His_Dark_Materials___1_" title="The Golden Compass (His Dark Materials, #1) by Philip Pullman" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Compass</a> counts. This may not be my genre. I am willing to keep going for a book or two, but the prospects are poor. And according to the clerk at the bookstore, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6381205.Soulless__The_Parasol_Protectorate___1_" title="Soulless (The Parasol Protectorate, #1) by Gail Carriger" rel="nofollow noopener">Soulless</a> <i>must</i> be my next read.<br /><br />I was on the fence about reading this one. It was officially on my to-read list, but the ho-hum reviews were making me doubt the placement. Then I heard Cherie Priest was coming to a local bookstore, Murder by the Book (great name, right?) in a week. I thought “better now rather than later”.<br /><br />Now I’ve read it. My feelings are best conveyed by shrugging my shoulders. It reminds me of young adult fiction: action at the expense of everything else. Good ideas get lost. Characters are encouragingly introduced, but never developed. There is no grander picture or underlying meaning. It is just a bit of fun. Sadly, it wasn't exactly my type of fun and I felt bored at times. To her credit, however, I did very much like the alternate world she created. And I marked a few pages for good descriptions.<br /><br />Let’s move on to the good stuff: meeting Cherie Priest. The book earned an extra star due to these fond memories. Honestly, she was more entertaining than her book.<br /><br />She was completely unscripted, which was <i>awesome</i>. She stood in front of thirty people and gossiped/joked/rambled for over an hour. She didn’t have notes or a plan. She didn’t read from her latest release. She talked about her mom’s crazy religious ideas. She made big gestures with her hands and talked too fast. She would lose her place mid-sentence and just start talking about something else. She wondered out aloud why her supermodel friend’s parents are so plain-looking. She was momentarily distracted when the store dog snored behind her (“The dog just snored behind me!”). In short, she was endearing. <br /><br />She talked candidly about how Boneshaker (with its great cover artwork) revived her career. She was under contract with Tor for four books. Her first three Southern Gothic Eden Moore books began as a mediocre success and then went downhill. She believes she could have sold more copies of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1137221.Not_Flesh_Nor_Feathers__Eden_Moore___3_" title="Not Flesh Nor Feathers (Eden Moore, #3) by Cherie Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">Not Flesh Nor Feathers</a> from the trunk of her car. She was certain Tor would drop her after the fourth book and was considering taking up a pen name for a fresh start. She took offense to some snobby, online comments that only the British could write steampunk because only the British had class issues, colonialism, an industrial revolution, wars, and so forth. She took up the challenge. She thought about how the American Civil War could be been dragged out if this happened, then this, and then that. Think of the new technologies that might have been created! Her editor had Cherie drop a vampire book in progress and devote her attention to this new idea. <br /><br />Nowadays, she has plans to keep writing in her alternate Clockwork Century world, including books set in New Orleans, Florida, and Washington DC. She would love to solve the Seattle problem one day. She has other projects too: collaborating with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R. R. Martins</a>(!), her new book about an OCD vampire <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8140731.Bloodshot__The_Cheshire_Red_Reports___1_" title="Bloodshot (The Cheshire Red Reports, #1) by Cherie Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloodshot</a>, and so forth. She is a ball of energy. <br /><br />She also explained why the connector book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670800.Clementine__The_Clockwork_Century___2_" title="Clementine (The Clockwork Century, #2) by Cherie Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">Clementine</a> is so hard to find: Tor didn’t want it. If she kept the book short, she could get around her contract with Tor and publish with her employer, Subterranean. They didn’t print enough initially. Cherie joked even she wouldn’t pay the $150 e-bay price for Clementine. There are now plans to print more.<br /><br />As usual, the best thing about meeting an author is that it helps me to better understand the tone of their books. Remember I wrote that Boneshaker was all action action action? I realized while listening to Cherie talk and crack jokes that she is okay with that. She wants to have fun. She likes throwing outrageous ideas together just because she can. More power to her. But I am moving on.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6843132328336388043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87243959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3932373866072784">I really wanted to like this one - my first real foray into steampunk, which I've always found aesthetically amusing, at least - but somehow, it just didn't do it for me. <br/><br/>I mean, it's bursting with cool stuff and sounds like it should be really fun to read: a brilliant mad scientist, an inventor of a clockwork horror that ravaged a city; an isolated alternate Seatlle surrounded by a giant wall that keeps in a deadly gas; said gas turns people into flesh-hungry zombies; the only way to get over s</span>
  <span id="freeText3932373866072784" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this one - my first real foray into steampunk, which I've always found aesthetically amusing, at least - but somehow, it just didn't do it for me. <br /><br />I mean, it's bursting with cool stuff and sounds like it should be really fun to read: a brilliant mad scientist, an inventor of a clockwork horror that ravaged a city; an isolated alternate Seatlle surrounded by a giant wall that keeps in a deadly gas; said gas turns people into flesh-hungry zombies; the only way to get over said wall is via a Final Fantasy-style airship; a collection of hardscrabble survivalists like the gruff lady bartender with the mechanical arm and the giant enforcer covered head to toe in elaborate armor.<br /><br />But somehow, none of this really <i>grabbed</i> me. I just kept reading, looking out for the next cool idea (the villain's lair is an interconnected series of train cars, buried underground!), but not getting involved in the story, which includes a fairly pedestrian mystery (who is the evil mad scientist?) and two dull leads (a mother's quest to save her son can probably be an interesting structure upon which to hang a zombie airship novel, but it would require interesting characters).<br /><br />I don't quite get it. Priest is a fine writer, and the plot clips along, but I just found a lot of it tedious, and the "solution" to the central mystery really fizzles. <br /><br />Plus I have <i>no idea</i> what I'm going to say when we discuss this in book club. It's not exactly deep in any sense of the word, just a fun (or not so fun, sadly) adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3932373866072784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_444846345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/444846345" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444846345?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=moments-of-great-frustration">moments-of-great-frustration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=pan-macmillan">pan-macmillan</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=zombies-zombies-everywhere">zombies-zombies-everywhere</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444846345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12768025376129374477">Is there anything a mother wouldn’t do to save her son? Even if they are mostly estranged and angry at each other? Would she willingly walk into a place where the air is poisonous and hundreds of zombies roam about? <br/><br/>Of course she would. I would, too. <br/><br/>That’s the choice Briar is forced to make, and it really isn’t a choice at all. Sixteen years ago, Seattle was destroyed by one of her late husband’s inventions, and she became an outcast, a poor, single mother with no one to rely on. From that poin</span>
  <span id="freeText12768025376129374477" style="display:none">Is there anything a mother wouldn’t do to save her son? Even if they are mostly estranged and angry at each other? Would she willingly walk into a place where the air is poisonous and hundreds of zombies roam about? <br><br>Of course she would. I would, too. <br><br>That’s the choice Briar is forced to make, and it really isn’t a choice at all. Sixteen years ago, Seattle was destroyed by one of her late husband’s inventions, and she became an outcast, a poor, single mother with no one to rely on. From that point on, Briar and her son were lucky when they could cross the street without someone spitting on them for something neither of them played any part in. <br>Briar’s son Zeke is only sixteen and he’s desperate to clear his father’s name, not knowing that his father really is guilty of turning Seattle into a poisonous prison. And there is no doubt in Briar’s mind, her late husband poisoned the air, flattened the city and created rotters, the zombies. But every boy wants his father to be perfect, so Zeke runs away from home to go to Seattle and prove his father’s innocence.<br><br>As much as I enjoyed the (too few) steampunk elements in Boneshaker, what I found most intriguing was the complexity of Briar’s relationship with her teenage son Zeke. I normally dislike situations that stem from lack of communication between characters, but in Boneshaker, their reasons for not sharing secrets with each other were so painful and real that I couldn’t blame Cherie Priest for deciding to write it exactly like that. It is what made these characters truly alive, as if they didn’t exist until they were around each other or thinking about each other. Despite the alternate history setting and all those fantastic inventions, despite the zombies and everything else that was exciting, Briar and Zeke were what really kept me on the edge of my seat. When it comes to character bulding, Cherie Priest is the best psychologist I’ve come across since Ann Aguirre, which is saying something, my friends. <br><br>But it appears that everything good comes at a price, and excellent characterization was very pricey indeed. In terms of steampunk, Boneshaker leaves a lot to be desired. I realize I’m very nitpicky when it comes to this sub-genre, but if authors won’t use the endless possibilities it provides, I see no point in writing it at all. The steampunk bits did not blow me away like they did in Ministry of Peculiar Occurrences, and I expected more from Priest language-wise, to be honest. Still, keep in mind that Boneshaker won the 2010 Locus Award for Science-Fiction, so this is probably just me being unreasonable and difficult. I get like that sometimes, just ask my siblings. :)<br><br>Although Boneshaker didn’t leave me completely satisfied, I am intrigued and eager to read the next book in this series. <br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11427319860740552471">My reaction to this book:<br/><br/>70% Really? But nothing has really happened!<br/>85% This is really quite boring<br/>87% Oh God, go away<br/>90% Maybe I should DNF?<br/>95% Somebody shoot me before I have to finish this<br/>99% There's a freaking EPILOGUE?!?! I won't survive...<br/><br/>Well clearly I survived, but I do have to say that it takes a special book to turn steampunk and zombies into boredom. And I can't even imagine making 90% and DNFing. Until now.<br/><br/>Anyway, I found the story boring and predictable and I didn't like the altern</span>
  <span id="freeText11427319860740552471" style="display:none">My reaction to this book:<br /><br />70% Really? But nothing has really happened!<br />85% This is really quite boring<br />87% Oh God, go away<br />90% Maybe I should DNF?<br />95% Somebody shoot me before I have to finish this<br />99% There's a freaking EPILOGUE?!?! I won't survive...<br /><br />Well clearly I survived, but I do have to say that it takes a special book to turn steampunk and zombies into boredom. And I can't even imagine making 90% and DNFing. Until now.<br /><br />Anyway, I found the story boring and predictable and I didn't like the alternating mother/son chapters. I've been looking forward to this one for a long time, too. You just never know.</span>
